The league announced the plans on Friday, setting the date for Saturday, Aug. 2, 2025.\n\n\"Major League Baseball is excited to deliver a special game at Bristol Motor Speedway, a unique setting that sports fans will remember forever,\" MLB Commisioner Rob Manfred said. \"The Reds and the Braves form an ideal matchup because of their dynamic talent and the proximity of their markets. (Sunday will be observed as an off day for both clubs.)\n\nBristol Motor Speedway is located near the Tennessee/Virginia state line and about 90 miles north of Asheville, North Carolina. It seats approximately 150,000 fans for NASCAR events and has rarely hosted non-motorsport events. In 2016, Tennessee and Virginia Tech played a college football game on the infield that drew 156,990 fans, a record for an NCAA football game. This year's game will feature the Tigers and New York Yankees on Aug. 18.\n\nAs non-division rivals, the Braves and Reds are scheduled to play two series in 2025: May 5-8 in Atlanta and Aug. 1-3 in Cincinnati/Bristol.\n\nThe largest crowd ever for an MLB game is 115,300 for an exhibition game between the Boston Red Sox and Los Angeles Dodgers at the Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum on March 29, 2008. The game will air on FOX at 7:00 p.m. ET.\n\nAn MLB-ready ballpark will be built across the infield of the famous race track where NASCAR has seen some of its most famous races take place.\n\nThe race, sponsored by BuildSubmarines.com, is a collaboration between the fabled track and Major League Baseball, with the possibility of NASCAR/MLB cross-promotion. The game will be treated as a Reds home game with revenues reimbursed to the club to make up for any lost revenue if the game were hosted at Great American Ballpark. The Reds 2025 schedule will now see two games on Thursday and Friday in Cincinnati ahead of the special Saturday matchup at Bristol and Sunday being held as a potential rain makeup date.\n\nThe game has the capacity to host one of the largest crowds MLB crowds in decades. Since 2021, Bristol Motor Speedway has had a seating capacity of 146,000. MLB has partnered with BaAM Productions, BrightView and Populous for the special event.\n\nMLB began looking at Bristol several years ago as a potential location to host a regular season game.\n\nPre-sales for the Speedway Classic will begin this September and will include early access purchase opportunities for Atlanta Braves and Cincinnati Reds Season Ticket Members as well as Bristol Motor Speedway racing ticketholders. The public ticket offering is expected this December.\n\n\"Major League Baseball is excited to deliver a special game at Bristol Motor Speedway, a unique setting that sports fans will remember forever,\" said MLB commissioner Rob Manfred. \"The Reds and the Braves form an ideal matchup because of their dynamic talent and the proximity of their markets. We look forward to celebrating our game with a wide array of fans, both on and off the field throughout the weekend, and highlighting the rich traditions of sports, music and community in Tennessee and across the region.\"\n\n\"Tennessee has a remarkable history of hosting sporting events on the national stage, and we're honored to host the first Major League Baseball game of its kind in state history,\" said Tennessee Governor Bill Lee. \"Baseball is a great American brand that belongs in Tennessee, and we look forward to welcoming Reds and Braves fans to Bristol while ensuring continued economic growth and prosperity across the Volunteer State.\"\n\nThe MLB Speedway Classic follows in the footsteps of other specialty jewel events that MLB has leaned into since Rob Manfred assumed the position of commissioner including games at Fort Bragg, the MLB Little League Classic, The MLB Field Of Dreams game, MLB at Omaha for the College World Series, the London Series, and most recently, the Rickwood Field: A Tribute To The Negro Leagues event.\n\n\"On behalf of the team at Bristol Motor Speedway and Speedway Motorsports, we are thrilled to partner with Major League Baseball to bring the Speedway Classic to the 'Home of Big Events'...,\" said Jerry Caldwell, President and General Manager of Bristol Motor Speedway. \"There is deep baseball history in Bristol and around this area, long acknowledged as the heart of the Appalachian League. In addition, Bristol's location makes it the perfect 'meet in the middle' destination for a showdown between these two beloved clubs. It's only appropriate for the World's Fastest Half-Mile to showcase this game where the talented athletes will be on display in a venue that's reputation was built on speed and high performance.\"\n\nThe last stick and ball event hosted at Bristol Motor Speedway was two college football games in consecutive weeks in 2016 between Tennessee-Virginia Tech and East Tennessee-Western Carolina. Motor Speedway next August", "body": "Major League Baseball is coming to Bristol Motor Speedway with the Braves and the Reds taking part in the Speedway Classic in August 2025\n\nFasten your seat belts, Major League Baseball is coming to Bristol Motor Speedway.\n\nOfficials from MLB and the track known as the \"Thunder Valley\" that holds more than 146,000 fans for NASCAR races announced Friday that the Atlanta Braves and Cincinnati Reds will play in the Speedway Classic there on Aug. 2, 2025.\n\nAn outline of where the field will be next summer was laid out on Bristol's infield with replica NASCAR machines, one with Atlanta's logo and the other with Cincinnati's logo.\n\nHall of Famer Chipper Jones of Atlanta threw out a ceremonial first pitch alongside NASCAR Hall of Famer Kevin Harvick, while Reds great Eric Davis was joined by racers Chase Elliott and Ross Chastain for their throw.\n\nIt will be a Reds home game with the first two being played at Cincinnati.\n\nMajor League Baseball has sought out and played games in different locations like the Field of Dreams games in Iowa, earlier this year in Birmingham, Alabama, to celebrate Negro League baseball and overseas in London the past several years.\n\nBristol, located in northeastern Tennessee on the state's border with Virginia, fits into that mission and gives those who can't always get to a baseball game a chance to see how the game has evolved, said Jeremiah Yolkut, MLB vice president of global events.\n\n\"To be able to bring the game here to Bristol and create storylines that tie into a faster paced game, high energy and big moments, this is the stage that we want to put that on,\" Yolkut said.\n\nTennessee Gov. Bill Lee, on hand at the track for the announcement, said Bristol is an iconic venue that has hosted pro and college football in its past, along with some of the most exciting NASCAR races on its 0.533-mile oval.\n\n\"History will be made when you have a special game here,\" Lee said.\n\nThe game will be the first National League or American League regular-season game played in the Volunteer State and continues MLB's push to break new ground. There have been major league games in recent seasons at MLB at Fort Bragg in 2016, MLB in Omaha in 2019, MLB at Field of Dreams in 2021, and MLB at Rickwood Field earlier this year.\n\nThose games were the first NL/AL contests in North Carolina, Nebraska, Iowa and Alabama.\n\n\"Major League Baseball is excited to deliver a special game at Bristol Motor Speedway, a unique setting that sports at Bristol.\n\n\"I never thought I'd see an infield of a NASCAR track, especially this one, knowing all these haulers are packed here like sardines,\" said Jones, elected to the Hall of Fame in 2018.\n\nElliott, the 2020 Cup Series champion and a big Braves fan, drove the Atlanta car for a few laps, dueling racing competitor Chastain in the Cincinnati car.\n\nElliott won an All-Star race at Bristol in 2020 and wants to come back in a year for the game. \"I just hope I can make it,\" said Elliott, the 2020 NASCAR Cup Series champion.\n\nThat might be a big ask since NASCAR is likely running that August weekend, although the schedule has yet to be announced.\n\nHarvick, the Hall of Famer, had no doubt that fans who fill the stands for racing will be just as supportive when the Bill Lee, on hand at the track for the announcement, said Bristol is an iconic venue that has hosted pro and college football in its past, along with some of the most exciting NASCAR races on its 0.533-mile oval.\n\n\"History will be made when you have a special game here,\" Lee said.\n\nThe game will be the first National League or American League regular-season game played in the Volunteer State and continues MLB's push to break new ground. There have been major league games in recent seasons at MLB at Fort Bragg in 2016, MLB in Omaha in 2019, MLB at Field of Dreams in 2021, and MLB at Rickwood Field earlier this year.\n\nThose games were the first NL/AL contests in North Carolina, Nebraska, Iowa and Alabama.\n\n\"Major League Baseball is excited to deliver a special game at Bristol Motor Speedway, a unique setting that sports at Bristol.\n\n\"I never thought I'd see an infield of a NASCAR track, especially this one, knowing all these haulers are packed here like sardines,\" said Jones, elected to the Hall of Fame in 2018.\n\nElliott, the 2020 Cup Series champion and a big Braves fan, drove the Atlanta car for a few laps, dueling racing competitor Chastain in the Cincinnati car.\n\nElliott won an All-Star race at Bristol in 2020 and wants to come back in a year for the game. \"I just hope I can make it,\" said Elliott, the 2020 NASCAR Cup Series champion.\n\nThat might be a big ask since NASCAR is likely running that August weekend, although the schedule has yet to be announced.\n\nHarvick, the Hall of Famer, had no doubt that fans who fill the stands for racing will be just as supportive when the Reds and Braves arrive.\n\nHarvick remembers the \"Battle of Bristol\" in 2016 when college football powers Tennessee and Virginia Tech played at the track in front of a record 156,990 the Negro American League's history and became a tribute to legendary Giants center fielder Willie Mays, who died two days before.\n\nThe Cardinals ended up coming out victorious defeating the Giants {"uri": "8267396144", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-09", "time": "17:33:39", "dateTime": "2024-08-09T17:33:39Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-09T17:33:08Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7529411911964417, "url": "https://www.oann.com/newsroom/mlb-will-host-braves-reds-in-first-ever-game-at-a-nascar-track-for-mlb-speedway-classic/", "title": "MLB Will Host Braves, Reds In First Ever Game At A NASCAR Track For 'MLB Speedway Classic'", "body": "Major League Baseball fans can rev up their engines as the league announced on Friday that NASCAR's famous Bristol Motor Speedway in Bristol, Tennessee, will host a regular-season MLB game for the first time-ever next year.\n\nThe game will take place on August 2, 2025, between the Atlanta Braves and the Cincinnati Reds, making it the first regular season MLB game to be held in Tennessee.\n\n\"We look forward to celebrating our game with a wide array of fans, both on and off the field throughout the weekend, and highlighting the rich traditions of sports, music and community in Tennessee and across the region,\" MLB Commissioner Rob Manfred said in a statement.\n\nThe Bristol Motor Speedway holds almost 150,000 people, making it one of the largest sporting venues. Next years ballgame will most likely break the single-game attendance record for a Major League Baseball game.\n\nCurrently, the Guinness World Record for largest ever attended baseball game was in 2008, during an exhibition game at the Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum between the Los Angeles Dodgers and the Boston Red Sox. There were 115,300 fans in attendance.\n\nThe average MLB stadium can hold between 40,000 to 45,000 fans.\n\nThis announcement comes as Major League Baseball has continued to expand the product across America and overseas. The MLB has hosted games in many nontraditional ballparks, including in 2016 when a game was held on an active military base in Fort Bragg, North Carolina and in 2021, when they had the Chicago White Sox play the New York Yankees on the iconic \"Field of Dreams\" in Dyersville, Iowa.\n\nIn June, the league hosted the \"MLB at Rickwood Field: A Tribute to the Negro Leagues\" in Birmingham, Alabama, two days after the death of Hall of Famer, Willie Mays.\n\nAdditionally, the MLB has slated multiple international cities to host games that include Tokyo, Mexico City, Paris, and San Juan, Puerto Rico, all in the 2025 season.\n\nThe Bristol Motor Speedway has hosted other events in the past, such as an NFL exhibition game in 1961. In 2016, Tennessee and Virginia Tech played in the \"Battle at Bristol\" that had 156,990 fans in attendance, which brought in the largest crowd ever to watch an NCAA football game.\n\nStay informed! {"uri": "2024-08-449590704", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-09", "time": "18:17:39", "dateTime": "2024-08-09T18:17:39Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-09T13:56:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7411764860153198, "url": "https://www.usnews.com/news/sports/articles/2024-08-09/rev-it-up-mlb-to-hold-braves-reds-game-at-bristol-motor-speedway-next-august", "title": "Rev It Up: MLB to Hold Braves-Reds Game at Bristol Motor Speedway Next August", "body": "Fasten your seat belts, Major League Baseball is coming to Bristol Motor Speedway.\n\nOfficials from MLB and the track known as the \"Thunder Valley\" that holds more than 146,000 fans for NASCAR races announced Friday that the Atlanta Braves and Cincinnati Reds will play in the Speedway Classic there on Aug. 2, 2025.\n\nAn outline of where the field will be next summer was laid out on Bristol's infield with replica NASCAR machines, one with Atlanta's logo and the other with Cincinnati's logo.\n\nHall of Famer Chipper Jones of Atlanta threw out a ceremonial first pitch alongside NASCAR Hall of Famer Kevin Harvick, while Reds great Eric Davis was joined by racers Chase Elliott and Ross Chastain for their throw.\n\nIt will be a Reds home game with the first two being played at Cincinnati.\n\nMajor League Baseball has sought out and played games in different locations like the Field of Dreams games in Iowa, earlier this year in Birmingham, Alabama, to celebrate Negro League baseball and overseas in London the past several years.\n\nBristol, located in northeastern Tennessee on the state's border with Virginia, fits into that mission and gives those who can't always get to a baseball game a chance to see how the game has evolved, said Jeremiah Yolkut, MLB vice president of global events.\n\n\"To be able to bring the game here to Bristol and create storylines that tie into a faster paced game, high energy and big moments, this is the stage that we want to put that on,\" Yolkut said.\n\nTennessee Gov. Bill Lee, on hand at the track for the announcement, said Bristol is an iconic venue that has hosted pro and college football in its past, along with some of the most exciting NASCAR races on its 0.533-mile oval.\n\n\"History will be made when you have a special game here,\" Lee said.\n\nThe game will be the first National League or American League regular-season game played in the Volunteer State and continues MLB's push to break new ground. There have been major league games in recent seasons at MLB at Fort Bragg in 2016, MLB in Omaha in 2019, MLB at Field of Dreams in 2021, and MLB at Rickwood Field earlier this year.\n\nThose games were the first NL/AL contests in North Carolina, Nebraska, Iowa and Alabama.\n\n\"Major League Baseball is excited to deliver a special game at Bristol Motor Speedway, a unique setting that sports fans will remember forever,\" said MLB commissioner Rob Manfred, also on hand for the announcement.\n\nJones, who played his entire big league career with the Braves, was wowed thinking about a game at Bristol.\n\n\"I never thought I'd see an infield of a NASCAR track, especially this one, knowing all these haulers are packed here like sardines,\" said Jones, elected to the Hall of Fame in 2018.\n\nElliott, the 2020 Cup Series champion and a big Braves fan, drove the Atlanta car for a few laps, dueling racing competitor Chastain in the Cincinnati car.\n\nElliott won an All-Star race at Bristol in 2020 and wants to come back in a year for the game. \"I just hope I can make it,\" said Elliott, the 2020 NASCAR Cup Series champion.\n\nThat might be a big ask since NASCAR is likely running that August weekend, although the schedule has yet to be announced.\n\nHarvick, the Hall of Famer, had no doubt that fans who fill the stands for racing will be just as supportive when the Reds and Braves arrive.\n\nHarvick remembers the \"Battle of Bristol\" in 2016 when college football powers Tennessee and Virginia Tech played at the track in front of a record 156,990 spectators.\n\n\"I think people are going be surprised at the size of what we would call a short track and now we're going to put a baseball field in the infield,\" Harvick said.\n\nCopyright 2024 The Associated Press. {"uri": "8267444611", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-09", "time": "18:18:03", "dateTime": "2024-08-09T18:18:03Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-09T18:16:40Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7411764860153198, "url": "https://wtop.com/national/2024/08/rev-it-up-mlb-to-hold-braves-reds-game-at-bristol-motor-speedway-next-august/", "title": "Rev It Up: MLB to hold Braves-Reds game at Bristol Motor Speedway next August - WTOP News", "body": "Fasten your seat belts, Major League Baseball is coming to Bristol Motor Speedway. Officials from MLB and the track known...\n\nFasten your seat belts, Major League Baseball is coming to Bristol Motor Speedway.\n\nOfficials from MLB and the track known as the \"Thunder Valley\" that holds more than 146,000 fans for NASCAR races announced Friday that the Atlanta Braves and Cincinnati Reds will play in the Speedway Classic there on Aug. 2, 2025.\n\nAn outline of where the field will be next summer was laid out on Bristol's infield with replica NASCAR machines, one with Atlanta's logo and the other with Cincinnati's logo.\n\nHall of Famer Chipper Jones of Atlanta threw out a ceremonial first pitch alongside NASCAR Hall of Famer Kevin Harvick, while Reds great Eric Davis was joined by racers Chase Elliott and Ross Chastain for their throw.\n\nIt will be a Reds home game with the first two being played at Cincinnati.\n\nMajor League Baseball has sought out and played games in different locations like the Field of Dreams games in Iowa, earlier this year in Birmingham, Alabama, to celebrate Negro League baseball and overseas in London the past several years.\n\nBristol, located in northeastern Tennessee on the state's border with Virginia, fits into that mission and gives those who can't always get to a baseball game a chance to see how the game has evolved, said Jeremiah Yolkut, MLB vice president of global events.\n\n\"To be able to bring the game here to Bristol and create storylines that tie into a faster paced game, high energy and big moments, this is the stage that we want to put that on,\" Yolkut said.\n\nTennessee Gov. Bill Lee, on hand at the track for the announcement, said Bristol is an iconic venue that has hosted pro and college football in its past, along with some of the most exciting NASCAR races on its 0.533-mile oval.\n\n\"History will be made when you have a special game here,\" Lee said.\n\nThe game will be the first National League or American League regular-season game played in the Volunteer State and continues MLB's push to break new ground. There have been major league games in recent seasons at MLB at Fort Bragg in 2016, MLB in Omaha in 2019, MLB at Field of Dreams in 2021, and MLB at Rickwood Field earlier this year.\n\nThose games were the first NL/AL contests in North Carolina, Nebraska, Iowa and Alabama.\n\n\"Major League Baseball is excited to deliver a special game at Bristol Motor Speedway, a unique setting that sports fans will remember forever,\" said MLB commissioner Rob Manfred, also on hand for the announcement.\n\nJones, who played his entire big league career with the Braves, was wowed thinking about a game at Bristol.\n\n\"I never thought I'd see an infield of a NASCAR track, especially this one, knowing all these haulers are packed here like sardines,\" said Jones, elected to the Hall of Fame in 2018.\n\nElliott, the 2020 Cup Series champion and a big Braves fan, drove the Atlanta car for a few laps, dueling racing competitor Chastain in the Cincinnati car.\n\nElliott won an All-Star race at Bristol in 2020 and wants to come back in a year for the game. \"I just hope I can make it,\" said Elliott, the 2020 NASCAR Cup Series champion.\n\nThat might be a big ask since NASCAR is likely running that August weekend, although the schedule has yet to be announced.\n\nHarvick, the Hall of Famer, had no doubt that fans who fill the stands for racing will be just as supportive when the Reds and Braves arrive.\n\nHarvick remembers the \"Battle of Bristol\" in 2016 when college football powers Tennessee and Virginia Tech played at the track in front of a record 156,990 spectators.\n\n\"I think people are going be surprised at the size of what we would call a short track and now we're going to put a baseball field in the infield,\" Harvick said.\n\nCopyright \u00a9 2024 The Associated Press. FOX will televise the historic game with a 7 p.m. ET start for next year's Saturday night event.\n\n\"Major League Baseball is excited to deliver a special game at Bristol Motor Speedway, a unique setting that sports fans will remember forever,\" MLB Commissioner Rob Manfred said. \"The Reds and the Braves form an ideal matchup because of their dynamic talent and the proximity of their markets.\n\n\"We look forward to celebrating our game with a wide array of fans, both on and off the field throughout the weekend, and highlighting the rich traditions of sports, music and community in Tennessee and across the region.\"\n\nThe record attendance for an MLB game is 115,300, set in March 2008 for an exhibition game between the Los Angeles Dodgers and Boston Red Sox at the Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum.\n\nWhether this event breaks that record (Bristol is not releasing a seating capacity for the game), is difficult to predict for a facility nestled in the Appalachian mountains that typically hosts drivers in race cars circling a high-banked 0.533-mile concrete oval.\n\nNext August, the only things reaching 100 miles an hour at Bristol will be baseballs. The game will serve as the finale of a three-game Reds homestand, with Friday and Saturday in Cincinnati. Sunday, May 3, will be held as a rain date, if needed.\n\nThis will be the first MLB game played in Tennessee, making it the fifth state since 2016 to play host to its first MLB contest.\n\nThe track is located in northeastern Tennessee, about 15 minutes from the unique Bristol main street that serves as the border of Tennessee and Virginia. The Bristol weekend will include live music in an area known for its deep roots in country music.\n\nAlthough the NASCAR schedule is not announced, typically Bristol has its big NASCAR weekends in the spring by mid-April and then again in September, leaving a few months for MLB to construct the field.\n\nMLB will use architectural design company Populous and landscape company BrightView to construct the field, partners it has used in the past for games such as the recent one at Rickwood Field in Birmingham, Ala.\n\nBristol will have to make some adjustments to its facility, removing part of its pit road wall and one of the buildings where tires are mounted on the wheels during the race weekend. The field dimensions will be 330 feet down the lines, 400 feet to center and 384 (left-center) and 375 (right-center) in the power alleys.\n\n\"There is deep baseball history in Bristol and around this area, long acknowledged as the heart of the Appalachian League,\" Bristol Motor Speedway general manager Jerry Caldwell said. \"In addition, Bristol's location makes it the perfect meet-in-the-middle destination for a showdown between these two beloved clubs.\"\n\nTicket prices were not announced as of Friday. is coming to Bristol Motor Speedway.\n\nOfficials from MLB and the track known as the \"Thunder Valley\" that holds more than 146,000 fans for NASCAR races announced Friday that the Atlanta Braves and Cincinnati Reds will play in the Speedway Classic there on Aug. 2, 2025.\n\nAn outline of where the field will be next summer was laid out on Bristol's infield with replica NASCAR machines, one with Atlanta's logo and the other with Cincinnati's logo.\n\nHall of Famer Chipper Jones of Atlanta threw out a ceremonial first pitch alongside NASCAR Hall of Famer Kevin Harvick, while Reds great Eric Davis was joined by racers Chase Elliott and Ross Chastain for their throw.\n\nIt will be a Reds home game with the first two being played at Cincinnati.\n\nMajor League Baseball has sought out and played games in different locations like the Field of Dreams games in Iowa, earlier this year in Birmingham, Alabama, to celebrate Negro League baseball and overseas in London the past several years.\n\nBristol, located in northeastern Tennessee on the state's border with Virginia, fits into that mission and gives those who can't always get to a baseball game a chance to see how the game has evolved, said Jeremiah Yolkut, MLB vice president of global events.\n\n\"To be able to bring the game here to Bristol and create storylines that tie into a faster paced game, high energy and big moments, this is the stage that we want to put that on,\" Yolkut said.\n\nTennessee Gov. Bill Lee, on hand at the track for the announcement, said Bristol is an iconic venue that has hosted pro and college football in its past, along with some of the most exciting NASCAR races on its 0.533-mile oval.\n\n\"History will be made when you have a special game here,\" Lee said.\n\nThe game will be the first National League or American League regular-season game played in the Volunteer State and continues MLB's push to break new ground. There have been major league games in recent seasons at MLB at Fort Bragg in 2016, MLB in Omaha in 2019, MLB at Field of Dreams in 2021, and MLB at Rickwood Field earlier this year.\n\nThose games were the first NL/AL contests in North Carolina, Nebraska, Iowa and Alabama.\n\n\"Major League Baseball is excited to deliver a special game at Bristol Motor Speedway, a unique setting that sports fans will remember forever,\" said MLB commissioner Rob Manfred, also on hand for the announcement.\n\nJones, who played his entire big league career with the Braves, was wowed thinking about a game at Bristol.\n\n\"I never thought I'd see an infield of a NASCAR track, especially this one, knowing all these haulers are packed here like sardines,\" said Jones, elected to the Hall of Fame in 2018.\n\nElliott, the 2020 Cup Series champion and a big Braves fan, drove the Atlanta car for a few laps, dueling racing competitor Chastain in the Cincinnati car.\n\nElliott won an All-Star race at Bristol in 2020 and wants to come back in a year for the game. \"I just hope I can make it,\" said Elliott, the 2020 NASCAR Cup Series champion.\n\nThat might be a big ask since NASCAR is likely running that August weekend, although the schedule has yet to be announced.\n\nHarvick, the Hall of Famer, had no doubt that fans who fill the stands for racing will be just as supportive when the Reds and Braves arrive.\n\nHarvick remembers the \"Battle of Bristol\" in 2016 when college football powers Tennessee and Virginia Tech played at the track in front of a record 156,990 spectators.\n\n\"I think people are going be surprised at the size of what we would call a short track and now we're going to put a baseball field in the infield,\" Harvick said.\n\nAP MLB: The track hosting a MLB game is not the first time Bristol will have hosted a high-profile event outside of motorsports, with Tennessee and Virginia Tech playing a college football game in 2016 on a purpose-built field in the infield. That game drew 156,990, the largest crowd ever to watch an NCAA football game.\n\nMeanwhile, MLB adds another venue to its growing lineup of special events. In recent years, the league has played regular season games in London, Mexico City, Tokyo and Seoul, in addition to Iowa for the Field of Dreams game, historic Rickwood Field in Birmingham, Ala. and Williamsport, Pa., site of the Little League World Series.\n\nMLB seems to have found an equally ambitious partner in Smith, whose company portfolio includes 10 tracks that host a combined 14 NASCAR Cup Series races. He is known within motorsports for grandiose ideas that fall outside conventional norms.\n\nIn addition to building a football field inside Bristol to host the Volunteers and Hokies, Smith also brought dirt in to completely cover Bristol's concrete racing surface in 2021 so that his track could host NASCAR's first premier series race on dirt since 1970. That experiment ended after three years. He also to great expense built a road course inside Charlotte Motor Speedway in 2018, his flagship facility. The venue currently hosts NASCAR's longest race, the Coca-Cola 600, on its 1.5-mile oval each Memorial Day weekend, then a playoff race on its 17-turn road course each fall.\n\nThis story will be (AP Photo/Marta Lavandier)\n\nBristol, located in northeastern Tennessee on the state's border with Virginia, fits into that mission and gives those who can't always get to a baseball game a chance to see how the game has evolved, said Jeremiah Yolkut, MLB vice president of global events.\n\n\"To be able to bring the game here to Bristol and create storylines that tie into a faster paced game, high energy and big moments, this is the stage that we want to put that on,\" Yolkut said.\n\nTennessee Gov. Bill Lee, on hand at the track for the announcement, said Bristol is an iconic venue that has hosted pro and college football in its past, along with some of the most exciting NASCAR races on its 0.533-mile oval.\n\n\"History will be made when you have a special game here,\" Lee said.\n\nThe game will be the first National League or American League regular-season game played in the Volunteer State and continues MLB's push to break new ground. There have been major league games in recent seasons at MLB at Fort Bragg in 2016, MLB in Omaha in 2019, MLB at Field of Dreams in 2021, and MLB at Rickwood Field earlier this year.\n\nThose games were the first NL/AL contests in North Carolina, Nebraska, Iowa and Alabama.\n\n\"Major League Baseball is excited to deliver a special game at Bristol Motor Speedway, a unique setting that sports fans will remember forever,\" said MLB commissioner Rob Manfred, also on hand for the announcement.\n\nJones, who played his entire big league career with the Braves, was wowed thinking about a game at Bristol.\n\n\"I never thought I'd see an infield of a NASCAR track, especially this one, knowing all these haulers are packed here like sardines,\" said Jones, elected to the Hall of Fame in 2018.\n\nElliott, the 2020 Cup Series champion and a big Braves fan, drove the Atlanta car for a few laps, dueling racing competitor Chastain in the Cincinnati car.\n\nElliott won an All-Star race at Bristol in 2020 and wants to come back in a year for the game. \"I just hope I can make it,\" said Elliott, the 2020 NASCAR Cup Series champion.\n\nThat might be a big ask since NASCAR is likely running that August weekend, although the schedule has yet to be announced.\n\nHarvick, the Hall of Famer, had no doubt that fans who fill the stands for racing will be just as supportive when the Reds and Braves arrive.\n\nHarvick remembers the \"Battle of Bristol\" in 2016 when college football powers Tennessee and Virginia Tech played at the track in front of a record 156,990 spectators.\n\n\"I think people are going be surprised at the size of what we would call a short track and now we're going to put a baseball field in the infield,\" Harvick said.\n\nAP MLB: Bill Lee.\n\nBristol baseball game field dimensions\n\nHere are the dimensions of what the baseball field will be at Bristol Motor Speedway.\n\nThe center field wall will be 400 feet from home plate.\n\nOther dimensions for the field for the 2025 Speedway Classic will be 330 feet down both right and left field. The distance to left center will be 384 feet and to right center 375 feet.\n\nLee joined Bristol Motor Speedway and MLB officials who made the official announcement for the game Friday at the 0.533-mile oval track. Seating will cover about two-thirds of the existing stands at the track.\n\nTemporary seats will be placed behind home plate and in the track's infield.\n\nThe field will be centered in the track's infield with home plate near the front straight away and center field near turn 2.\n\nMore than 160,000 tons of gravel will be brought in for construction of the field with two sets of drain systems installed. Presale starts in September.\n\nTennessee football played Virginia Tech at Bristol in 2016\n\nBristol Motor Speedway, which is home to two annual NASCAR races, served as host to the 2016 college football game between Tennessee and Virginia Tech. {"uri": "2024-08-449504179", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-09", "time": "16:33:40", "dateTime": "2024-08-09T16:33:40Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-09T16:32:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6901960968971252, "url": "https://www.washingtonpost.com/sports/2024/08/09/braves-reds-bristol-motor-speedway/", "title": "MLB will play a game inside a NASCAR speedway. How will that work?", "body": "Sorry, a summary is not available for this article at this time. Please try again later.\n\nAs potential baseball venues go, a NASCAR track located four hours from any current major league city is not the most intuitive target. But a major motor speedway will hold a major league baseball game all the same. MLB Commissioner Rob Manfred announced Friday that the Atlanta Braves will play the Cincinnati Reds at Bristol Motor Speedway in Bristol, Tenn., on Aug. 2, 2025, on a field built across the infield and track of one of NASCAR's most treasured and historic venues.\n\n\"If you look around here, or if you look online at what Bristol Motor Speedway is, it truly is a coliseum,\" MLB Vice President of Global Events Jeremiah Yokult said at a news conference Friday morning. \"And we felt when we walked into this place several years ago and we looked at it, that there was no better stage to consider putting on a large-scale event that would bring baseball onto the infield of a racetrack to further bring out what's so great about baseball.\"\n\nBristol Motor Speedway is located just south of the border between Virginia and Tennessee, a relative dead zone for Major League Baseball. The Braves (272 miles south) and Reds (302 miles northwest) are the teams whose homes are nearest the facility, with the Washington Nationals roughly 390 miles to the northeast.\n\nSignificantly, the facility is also within driving distance of Nashville, one of the primary contenders to be awarded a team when MLB next expands.\n\nMLB has long scheduled showcase games abroad. London trips are regular occurrences. The San Francisco Giants and San Diego Padres played a series in Mexico City last year. The Los Angeles Dodgers and Padres opened this regular season in Seoul, and the Dodgers and Chicago Cubs will open in Tokyo next year.\n\nBut in recent years, MLB has expanded its portfolio of domestic showcase games, playing the Field of Dreams games in Iowa and, most recently, playing a regular season game in June at historic Rickwood Field in Birmingham, Ala., to celebrate the legacy of Negro League players.\n\nIn some ways, then, Bristol Motor Speedway does not fit the pattern. It is not a landmark of baseball culture, such as Dyersville, Iowa, or a significant stage for baseball history, such as Rickwood. But it is different, and MLB officials have been adamant about the need to reach new groups with the game.\n\n\"What special event games do for us, when we bring them to different locales across the globe, is we're really able to amplify what baseball means to local communities and the storylines we're able to tell,\" Yokult said. \"... There are folks that don't always get to go to one of our 30 major league ballparks. So the idea is we can bring that product to places like Tennessee where it's very baseball rich, but they don't have the opportunity to see major league baseball all the time.\"\n\nTennessee Gov. Bill Lee said he expects \"hundreds of millions of dollars\" of economic boost from the event, which he called \"a big showcase for us.\" Indeed, if interest is high, plenty of fans will have the chance to attend. When it is configured for racing, Bristol Motor Speedway holds 146,000 people. When it hosted a college football game between locals Virginia Tech and Tennessee in 2016, it held 156,990.\n\nExactly how many people will be able to see the Reds and Braves next year remains to be seen, though early renderings of the setup suggest the part of the historic oval behind home plate will not be available for seating, with a smaller number of seats installed at ground level surrounding home plate.\n\nThe field itself has to be positioned just to the right of the massive several-sided hanging screen they call \"Colossus\" to avoid any batted balls hitting the board. Some low walls around the track will be removed, and thousands of tons of gravel will be brought into the infield and pit areas to create a surface level enough for major league field standards. The foul poles will be 330 feet from home plate down both lines, and center field will be 400 feet from home plate.\n\nIn terms of baseball scheduling logistics, the Saturday night game will count as a home game for the Reds and will be played after Thursday and Friday games between the teams in Cincinnati. Both teams will have a scheduled day off Sunday to allow the game to be rescheduled in case of inclement weather.\n\nThe game will be part of a much bigger weekend, one that will also include nods to Bristol's heritage as \"the birthplace of country music\" -- making for a far less baseball-centric event than other showcase games played at, for example, the home of the College World Series in Omaha in 2019.", "source": {"uri": "washingtonpost.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Washington Post"}, "authors": [{"uri": "chelsea_janes@washingtonpost.com", "name": "Chelsea Janes", "type": {"uri": "8267499396", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-09", "time": "19:08:11", "dateTime": "2024-08-09T19:08:11Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-09T19:07:28Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6705882549285889, "url": "https://www.chattanoogan.com/2024/8/9/490746/Braves-Reds-To-Play-1st-Major-League.aspx", "title": "Braves, Reds To Play 1st Major League Baseball Game In Tennessee Next Aug. 2", "body": "Governor Bill Lee announced Friday that the Cincinnati Reds and Atlanta Braves will play a regular season game in theMLB Speedway Classic at Tennessee's Bristol Motor Speedway on Saturday, Aug. 2, 2025.\n\nHe said, \"This historic announcement marks the first American or National League game played in Tennessee.\n\n\"Tennessee has a remarkable history of hosting sporting events on the national stage, and we're honored to announce the first Major League Baseball game of its kind in state history.\n\n\"Baseball is a great American brand that belongs in Tennessee, and we look forward to welcoming Reds and Braves fans to Bristol while ensuring continued economic growth and prosperity across the Volunteer State.\"\n\nThe MLB Speedway Classic is the second event to be awarded funding from the Special Event Fund. In 2022, Governor Lee partnered with the General Assembly to appropriate $25 million in the state budget for a fund designed to attract and retain high-profile events that deliver significant economic impact, create jobs, and showcase the state to a global audience. The Special Event Fund is a competitive, incentive-based grant program tied to measurable performance outcomes. Eligible events will generate direct economic impact greater than $10 million, and a net economic benefit of at least $1 million in state tax revenue.\n\n\"We are home to the best sports fans in the nation, and now they -- along with thousands of fans from around the globe -- will get to experience Major League Baseball here for the very first time,\" said Commissioner Mark Ezell, Tennessee Department of Tourist Development. \"This is a home run for Tennessee residents and visitors. It's a tremendous opportunity for our businesses and communities, and will no doubt be another landmark sporting event at Bristol Motor Speedway.\"\n\nA major league field will be constructed across the famed track at Bristol Motor Speedway, one of the largest sporting venues in the world.\n\nThe MLB Speedway Classic will include a range of festivities, including a musical presence in the \"birthplace of country music.\"\n\n\"Major League Baseball is excited to deliver a special game at Bristol Motor Speedway, a unique setting that sports fans will remember forever,\" said Robert D. Manfred, Jr., Commissioner of Baseball. \"The Reds and the Braves form an ideal matchup because of their dynamic talent and the proximity of their markets. We look forward to celebrating our game with a wide array of fans, both on and off the field throughout the weekend, and highlighting the rich traditions of sports, music, and community in Tennessee and across the region.\"\n\nOfficials said, \"As Tennessee's second largest industry, tourism is a significant contributor to the state's overall economic development and vitality. In 2023, tourism in Tennessee generated a record $30.6 billion in direct visitor pending, with 144 million visitors according to Tourism Economics. {"uri": "8267450494", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-09", "time": "18:23:06", "dateTime": "2024-08-09T18:23:06Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-09T18:21:51Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6666666865348816, "url": "https://heraldcourier.com/news/state-and-regional/rev-it-up-mlb-to-hold-braves-reds-game-at-bristol-motor-speedway-next-august/article_a445ee20-a34c-59b7-8476-73f076968287.html", "title": "Rev It Up: MLB to hold Braves-Reds game at Bristol Motor Speedway next August", "body": "By PETE IACOBELLI - AP Sports Writer\n\nFasten your seat belts, Major League Baseball is coming to Bristol Motor Speedway.\n\nOfficials from MLB and the track known as the \"Thunder Valley\" that holds more than 146,000 fans for NASCAR races announced Friday that the Atlanta Braves and Cincinnati Reds will play in the Speedway Classic there on Aug. 2, 2025.\n\nAn outline of where the field will be next summer was laid out on Bristol's infield with replica NASCAR machines, one with Atlanta's logo and the other with Cincinnati's logo.\n\nHall of Famer Chipper Jones of Atlanta threw out a ceremonial first pitch alongside NASCAR Hall of Famer Kevin Harvick, while Reds great Eric Davis was joined by racers Chase Elliott and Ross Chastain for their throw.\n\nIt will be a Reds home game with the first two being played at Cincinnati.\n\nPeople are also reading... Memories lead many to Lebanon's Bonanza Steakhouse HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: Not yet 30, Norris achieves goal as Lebanon head coach PREP VOLLEYBALL: Four-time defending region champ Gate City will have new coach this season as Reed steps down Platter & Pour working to open State Street location HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL | Trust and obey: Former Sullivan East star Laisure now playing for Science Hill Hilltoppers PREP BASKETBALL: Field released for The Classic at Tennessee High PREP FOOTBALL: J.I. Burton looking for Raider revival after struggles of 2023 Antiques showcased at Virginia Highlands Festival HIGH SCHOOL NOTEBOOK: Wise Central's Emmah McAmis on Under Armour national title team; Some transfers and new coaching hires as well HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: Smith aims high for Ridgeview LOCAL MOTORSPORTS: Chilhowie racer knows the Bristol Motor Speedway experience VHSL PRESEASON FOOTBALL PRIMER: Plenty of storylines as prep football begins in Virginia PREP FOOTBALL: Wise County Central's Owen Amos returns from injury BRIEFS: Tommy Buzzo steps down as E&H's defensive coordinator Trail town now boasts pathway lined with artwork\n\nMajor League Baseball has sought out and played games in different locations like the Field of Dreams games in Iowa, earlier this year in Birmingham, Alabama, to celebrate Negro League baseball and overseas in London the past several years.\n\nBristol, located in northeastern Tennessee on the state's border with Virginia, fits into that mission and gives those who can't always get to a baseball game a chance to see how the game has evolved, said Jeremiah Yolkut, MLB vice president of global events.\n\n\"To be able to bring the game here to Bristol and create storylines that tie into a faster paced game, high energy and big moments, this is the stage that we want to put that on,\" Yolkut said.\n\nTennessee Gov. Bill Lee, on hand at the track for the announcement, said Bristol is an iconic venue that has hosted pro and college football in its past, along with some of the most exciting NASCAR races on its 0.533-mile oval.\n\n\"History will be made when you have a special game here,\" Lee said.\n\nThe game will be the first National League or American League regular-season game played in the Volunteer State and continues MLB's push to break new ground. There have been major league games in recent seasons at MLB at Fort Bragg in 2016, MLB in Omaha in 2019, MLB at Field of Dreams in 2021, and MLB at Rickwood Field earlier this year.\n\nThose games were the first NL/AL contests in North Carolina, Nebraska, Iowa and Alabama.\n\n\"Major League Baseball is excited to deliver a special game at Bristol Motor Speedway, a unique setting that sports fans will remember forever,\" said MLB commissioner Rob Manfred, also on hand for the announcement.\n\nJones, who played his entire big league career with the Braves, was wowed thinking about a game at Bristol.\n\n\"I never thought I'd see an infield of a NASCAR track, especially this one, knowing all these haulers are packed here like sardines,\" said Jones, elected to the Hall of Fame in 2018.\n\nElliott, the 2020 Cup Series champion and a big Braves fan, drove the Atlanta car for a few laps, dueling racing competitor Chastain in the Cincinnati car.\n\nElliott won an All-Star race at Bristol in 2020 and wants to come back in a year for the game. \"I just hope I can make it,\" said Elliott, the 2020 NASCAR Cup Series champion.\n\nThat might be a big ask since NASCAR is likely running that August weekend, although the schedule has yet to be announced.\n\nHarvick, the Hall of Famer, had no doubt that fans who fill the stands for racing will be just as supportive when the Reds and Braves arrive.\n\nHarvick remembers the \"Battle of Bristol\" in 2016 when college football powers Tennessee and Virginia Tech played at the track in front of a record 156,990 spectators.\n\n\"I think people are going be surprised at the size of what we would call a short track and now we're going to put a baseball field in the infield,\" Harvick said.\n\nAP MLB: https://apnews.com/hub/mlb\n\nAP NASCAR: https://apnews.com/hub/nascar-racing\n\nCopyright 2024 The Associated Press. Don't worry, NASCAR isn't running a race in the middle of a Los Angeles Dodgers game. Major League Baseball announced on Friday that Bristol Motor Speedway will host the MLB Speedway Classic, a regular-season game between the Atlanta Braves and the Cincinnati Reds in 2025.\n\nThe high-banked half-mile short track in Eastern Tennessee first hosted the NASCAR Cup Series in 1961 and remains a schedule staple. A typical race weekend sees team haulers shuffled into the infield door-to-door like a game of Tetris. Next year's August 5 matchup will see the infield transformed into a ballpark with the speedway's suspended jumbotron dangling outside of the left field foul line over a grandstand.\n\nLiving up to the venue's nickname, \"The Last Great Coliseum,\" MLB's goal is likely to fill as many of Bristol's 146,000 seats as possible. However, the event's renderings show a pretty dull field configuration despite baseball's rules allowing for extremely quirky dimensions. I want to see the outfielders contending with the 24-degree banking to catch fly balls. I want to see the catch fence as part of the outfield wall.\n\nRob Manfred, the Commissioner of Baseball and contender for most-hated man in sports, said in statement:\n\n\"Major League Baseball is excited to deliver a special game at Bristol Motor Speedway, a unique setting that sports fans will remember forever. The Reds and the Braves form an ideal matchup because of their dynamic talent and the proximity of their markets. We look forward to celebrating our game with a wide array of fans, both on and off the field throughout the weekend, and highlighting the rich traditions of sports, music and community in Tennessee and across the region.\"\n\nProfessional sports leagues are always looking for a new spectacle, but there has been an uptick in recent years. NASCAR moved the Busch Clash to the Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum. For its part, MLB plays a two-game regular-season series in London.\n\nThe inspiration for the Speedway Classic was the Battle at Bristol, a college football game between Tennessee and Virginia Tech. The 2016 event shattered records with 156,990 fans in attendance. The game's success was attributed to the race track being a natural neutral site near the Tennessee-Virginia state line, the South's love for college football and the season is only 12 games longer. Fan seating will run across about two-thirds of the existing Bristol stands, fanning out around the outfield. A smaller set of stands will be built right behind homeplate and the infield.\n\nTickets go on sale in early December. Presale for race fans starts in September.\n\n\"For me, and our state, it gives a picture to Americans of how remarkable or how unique it is here,\" Lee said. \"When we have these global sports events, the world sees what we know in Tennessee.\"\n\nOrganizers are betting fans of the Reds, Braves and NASCAR will travel to the special game.\n\n\"We're bringing major league baseball and auto racing together,\" NASCAR announcer Jamie Little said. \"And who wins? The fans.\"\n\nBraves legend Chipper Jones said he's excited to see the spectacle of a baseball game in the massive speedway.\n\n\"Being from the South, knowing what NASCAR means to everyone from the South (means a lot),\" Jones said. All professional athletes stand in awe of professional athletes in other sports. I stand in amazement of what these guys do.\"\n\nReds legend Eric Davis said the league's emphasis on speeding up games pairs with Bristol's famous half-mile banked track.\n\nMLB announced the Reds will be the home team for the game. The game will be on a Saturday with Sunday held as a potential rain date.\n\nMusic will play a role in Braves-Reds game\n\nBristol is known as the birthplace of country music, and a concert will be a part of the festivities.\n\n\"Big sporting events and music go hand in hand - nobody does music like Tennessee,\" Lee said.\n\nIt's a Bristol tradition, after all. Fields surrounding the track are transformed into a village of tents and vendors on race weekends.\n\nThe game will be a moneymaker for Tennessee\n\nLee said the game is expected to bring in $100 million to the Volunteer State.\n\n\"The ripple effects of that are hard to measure,\" Lee said. \"When people see the uniqueness of the state, it's good for Tennessee.\"\n\nHow are state officials preparing for the game?\n\nTennessee and MLB officials are expecting a full stadium. Making sure there's adequate infrastructure of an influx of people will be key, Lee said.\n\n\"We hold major sporting events and enormous crowds,\" Lee said. \"We know how to prepare for it, we know what public safety should look like. (People) want to know its going to be safe when they come here, they want to know it's going to be easy to get here and easy to get out.\"\n\nThe state will work with local officials who are used to hosting massive crowds in the vast, open fields surrounding the track on race weekends.\n\nBristol has a history of hosting events\n\nBristol's short track is home to annual NASCAR races, of course, and other races throughout the year.\n\nIn 2016, the Tennessee Vols played Virginia Tech in front of an audience of 156,990. It was the largest crowd ever at an NCAA football game.\n\nHow do they do it? Meticulous planning. They'll bring in 160,000 tons of gravel, two sets of drain systems and demolish and rebuild some of the track's walls to build netting to protect fans.\n\nBristol is under about 2 hours away from {"uri": "8267530004", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-09", "time": "19:37:42", "dateTime": "2024-08-09T19:37:42Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-09T19:36:22Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6117647290229797, "url": "https://heraldcourier.com/bms-to-serve-as-big-league-city-for-one-night-in-25/article_fb25cb12-5682-11ef-ab71-7f33f9701edd.html", "title": "BMS to serve as big league city for one night in '25", "body": "BRISTOL, Tenn. - Baseball has been played at various levels, venues and on both sides of the state line in Bristol for more than a century and the city will be big league for one evening next year.\n\nIt was officially announced on Friday in a press conference at Bristol Motor Speedway that the NASCAR track will host a Major League Baseball regular season game between the Atlanta Braves and Cincinnati Reds on Saturday, Aug. 2, 2025.\n\nThe event will be dubbed as the Speedway Classic and has been rumored for months.\n\nAnnouncer Chris Myers of FOX initially hinted publicly at the idea of BMS possibly hosting a Braves game during the broadcast of the NASCAR Cup Series Food City 500 in March. Meanwhile, Jordan Bianchi and Evan Drellich of the Athletic officially broke the story earlier in the week.\n\nIt's a go as the white flag has officially dropped - to borrow a racing metaphor - for the countdown.\n\nPeople are also reading... Memories lead many to Lebanon's Bonanza Steakhouse HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: Not yet 30, Norris achieves goal as Lebanon head coach PREP VOLLEYBALL: Four-time defending region champ Gate City will have new coach this season as Reed steps down Platter & Pour working to open State Street location HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL | Trust and obey: Former Sullivan East star Laisure now playing for Science Hill Hilltoppers PREP BASKETBALL: Field released for The Classic at Tennessee High PREP FOOTBALL: J.I. Burton looking for Raider revival after struggles of 2023 Antiques showcased at Virginia Highlands Festival HIGH SCHOOL NOTEBOOK: Wise Central's Emmah McAmis on Under Armour national title team; Some transfers and new coaching hires as well HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: Smith aims high for Ridgeview LOCAL MOTORSPORTS: Chilhowie racer knows the Bristol Motor Speedway experience VHSL PRESEASON FOOTBALL PRIMER: Plenty of storylines as prep football begins in Virginia PREP FOOTBALL: Wise County Central's Owen Amos returns from injury BRIEFS: Tommy Buzzo steps down as E&H's defensive coordinator Trail town now boasts pathway lined with artwork\n\nIt will be the first MLB regular-season game ever played in the state Tennessee and will mark the first time MLB teams will have visited Bristol since the Brooklyn Robins, New York Yankees (with Babe Ruth as the star slugger), New York Giants (featuring a future manager by the name of Casey Stengel), Chicago White Sox and Philadelphia Athletics (managed by Connie Mack) played a series of exhibition games at Tenneva Field from April 5-8, 1922.\n\nThis one will count in the standings with superstars such as Atlanta's Ronald Acuna Jr. and Cincinnati's Elly De La Cruz being among the most popular must-see players on the field this time around.\n\nThe game will be televised in primetime on FOX.\n\nThe exact time for first pitch has not been set yet (Cincinnati will be the home team), but officials said during Friday's press event that it will indeed be a night game. If rained out, the game would be played the following day according to Jeremiah Yolkut, MLB's vice president in charge of global events.\n\nThe VIPs at BMS on Friday included Baseball Hall of Famer and Braves legend Chipper Jones, along with Eric Davis who starred for the Cincinnati Reds when they won the 1990 World Series. MLB commissioner Rob Manfred did not make an appearance despite being scheduled to do so.\n\nHead baseball coaches from area high schools were invited with Sullivan East's Mike Breuninger, John Battle's Jimmy Gobble, Virginia High's Adam Moore and Providence Academy's Jeff Reed among those spotted in the large crowd. Gobble and Reed both played in the majors with Reed winning a World Series ring as a catcher with the Reds in 1990.\n\nMeanwhile, Chipper Jones was visiting Bristol Motor Speedway for the first time.\n\n\"Very exciting,\" Jones said. \"I know everybody in the Braves organization is crazy jacked to get here. On a personal note, this is a place I've held high on my bucket list for a very long time.\"\n\nThe game is being held in what players call the \"dog days\" of the season, but an event that will have all the feel of a postseason game could provide a major pick-me-up.\n\n\"The routine for a major league baseball player gets kind of monotonous,\" Jones said. \"You do it all day, every day. Very seldom do you have a day off. It's good to have something to kind of break the monotony and this is the perfect instance for that. ... Right around the end of July, start of August most guys will tell you they hit a wall for about a week or 10 days where they aren't quite themselves. I feel like a break from the everyday monotony to come up here and be a part of something as special as this - every guy on that roster is going to sign up for it I promise you.\"\n\nMLB, NFL and NBA exhibition games have been held in Bristol before.\n\nThere were those aforementioned 1922 MLB exhibitions at Tenneva Field, located on what is now Commonwealth Avenue where Strongwell Corporation sits.\n\nBristol's racetrack was the home of a 1961 NFL preseason game between the Washington Redskins and Philadelphia Eagles.\n\nA 1983 NBA preseason game between the Atlanta Hawks and Cleveland Cavaliers was contested at Viking Hall.\n\nThis will be a regular season game at Bristol Motor Speedway and could provide the venue a single-game attendance record in yet another sport.\n\nTennessee's 45-24 victory over Virginia Tech on Sept. 10, 2016, in the \"Battle at Bristol\" established a college football crowd record that still stands.\n\nThe MLB mark for single-game attendance is the 115,300 who showed up at the Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum for an exhibition game between the Boston Red Sox and Los Angeles Dodgers on March 29, 2008.\n\nA regular-season doubleheader between the Cleveland Indians and New York Yankees at Municipal Stadium in Ohio apparently brought in 86,563 fans on Sept. 12, 1954. Game 5 of the 1959 World Series in Los Angeles had 92,706 people come through the turnstiles.\n\nTennessee Governor Bill Lee said there was a \"probability\" and \"likelihood\" that Bristol would own the MLB mark by this time next year.\n\nIt also could provide more momentum for the growing cause to put an MLB expansion team in Nashville.\n\nHaving the area's two most popular teams and two closest big-league teams - Atlanta and Cincinnati -playing each other will certainly put butts in the seats.\n\nHere's one connection between the two franchises that showcase the area's rich baseball heritage.\n\nClyde \"Hardrock\" Shoun of Mountain City, Tennessee, pitched for five seasons for Cincinnati and three seasons with the Boston Braves in the 1940s.\n\nHe pitched a no-hitter for the Reds on May 15, 1944, against the Braves.\n\nThe Speedway Classic could also occur a week after another major baseball milestone for the area.\n\nFormer Tazewell High School star Billy Wagner is expected to be elected to the National Baseball Hall of Fame in 2025 - the fireballing relief pitcher missed enshrinement by five votes when the most recent ballots were unveiled in January - and induction day is set for July 27, 2025, in Cooperstown, New York.\n\nPerhaps the Southwest Virginia native could throw out the first pitch at BMS as he closed out his stellar 16-year big-league career with the Braves in 2010.\n\n\"I think it would be awesome to throw out the first pitch but I'm sure there are much better options,\" Wagner said on Thursday in a telephone interview.\n\nWagner had been to BMS before.\n\n\"Of course,\" Wagner said. \"Was a big fan of [NASCAR driver] Morgan Shepherd.\"\n\nCount him among those all in when it comes to baseball at BMS.\n\n\"Playing in front of that type of crowd will be electric,\" Wagner said.\n\nSouthwest Virginia native and ex-East Tennessee State University slugger Ed Goodson played 47 games for the Atlanta Braves in 1975 - sandwiched between stints with the San Francisco Giants and Los Angeles Dodgers during an eight-season career - and could make the trip from his home in Grayson County, Virginia.\n\n\"I have never been to any events there,\" Goodson said. \"I got to see it quite a few times on my trips to and from Ivanhoe [Virginia] to ETSU when I was in college. ... I would be interested in attending the game if I can get [son] Kirk [Goodson], my son-in-law, and my three grandsons to go.\"\n\nVirginia High graduate Justin Grimm won a World Series in 2010 while pitching for the Chicago Cubs and now lives in Nashville. He's saved the date.\n\n\"I love that MLB is bringing the game to the East Tennessee area,\" Grimm said. \"When I read about it, I had to do a double take and immediately text my brother [Matt] and told him to put it on the calendar. What a great way for our area to go watch a big-league ballgame.\"\n\nThe dimensions presented of the playing field on Friday included 330 feet down the lines as the diamond would be situated in one corner of the racing infield. Plenty of work is still yet to be done.\n\n\"It's going to be really fun to watch the transformation take place,\" Jones said.\n\nMLB has held regular season games at historic Rickwood Field in Birmingham, Alabama, the Field of Dreams in Dyersville, Iowa, and foreign countries in recent years.\n\nBristol Motor Speedway and Major League Baseball are attempting to turn quite a double play.\n\n\"You walk into the venue and right away you know you're in a different kind of place, something incredibly special,\" Yolkut said. \"Not only is it big on the outside, but the energy on the inside, even when it is empty, is different than any of the other places we've recently been.\"\n\nBe the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your inbox!\n\nSign up! * I understand and agree {"uri": "8267541132", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-09", "time": "19:48:35", "dateTime": "2024-08-09T19:48:35Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-09T19:47:50Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6000000238418579, "url": "https://heraldcourier.com/speedway-classic-adds-to-rich-local-history/article_fb25cb12-5682-11ef-ab71-7f33f9701edd.html", "title": "Speedway Classic adds to rich local history", "body": "Kevin Harvick (left), American semi-retired professional stock car driver and commentator for NASCAR on Fox, and Chipper Jones, retired MLB player for the Atlanta Braves, unveil the official pace car during Friday morning's press conference.\n\nTIM HAYES Bristol Herald Courier\n\nBRISTOL, Tenn. - Baseball has been played at various levels, venues and on both sides of the state line in Bristol for more than a century and the city will be big league for one evening next year.\n\nIt was officially announced on Friday in a press conference at Bristol Motor Speedway that the NASCAR track will host a Major League Baseball regular season game between the Atlanta Braves and Cincinnati Reds on Saturday, Aug. 2, 2025.\n\nThe event will be dubbed as the Speedway Classic and has been rumored for months.\n\nAnnouncer Chris Myers of FOX initially hinted publicly at the idea of BMS possibly hosting a Braves game during the broadcast of the NASCAR Cup Series Food City 500 in March. Meanwhile, Jordan Bianchi and Evan Drellich of the Athletic officially broke the story earlier in the week.\n\nIt's a go as the white flag has officially dropped - to borrow a racing metaphor - for the countdown.\n\nPeople are also reading... Memories lead many to Lebanon's Bonanza Steakhouse HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: Not yet 30, Norris achieves goal as Lebanon head coach PREP VOLLEYBALL: Four-time defending region champ Gate City will have new coach this season as Reed steps down Platter & Pour working to open State Street location HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL | Trust and obey: Former Sullivan East star Laisure now playing for Science Hill Hilltoppers PREP BASKETBALL: Field released for The Classic at Tennessee High PREP FOOTBALL: J.I. Burton looking for Raider revival after struggles of 2023 Antiques showcased at Virginia Highlands Festival HIGH SCHOOL NOTEBOOK: Wise Central's Emmah McAmis on Under Armour national title team; Some transfers and new coaching hires as well HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: Smith aims high for Ridgeview LOCAL MOTORSPORTS: Chilhowie racer knows the Bristol Motor Speedway experience VHSL PRESEASON FOOTBALL PRIMER: Plenty of storylines as prep football begins in Virginia PREP FOOTBALL: Wise County Central's Owen Amos returns from injury BRIEFS: Tommy Buzzo steps down as E&H's defensive coordinator Trail town now boasts pathway lined with artwork\n\nIt will be the first MLB regular-season game ever played in the state Tennessee and will mark the first time MLB teams will have visited Bristol since the Brooklyn Robins, New York Yankees (with Babe Ruth as the star slugger), New York Giants (featuring a future manager by the name of Casey Stengel), Chicago White Sox and Philadelphia Athletics (managed by Connie Mack) played a series of exhibition games at Tenneva Field from April 5-8, 1922.\n\nThis one will count in the standings with superstars such as Atlanta's Ronald Acuna Jr. and Cincinnati's Elly De La Cruz being among the most popular must-see players on the field this time around.\n\nThe game will be televised in primetime on FOX.\n\nThe exact time for first pitch has not been set yet (Cincinnati will be the home team), but officials said during Friday's press event that it will indeed be a night game. If rained out, the game would be played the following day according to Jeremiah Yolkut, MLB's vice president in charge of global events.\n\nThe VIPs at BMS on Friday included Baseball Hall of Famer and Braves legend Chipper Jones, along with Eric Davis who starred for the Cincinnati Reds when they won the 1990 World Series. MLB commissioner Rob Manfred did not make an appearance despite being scheduled to do so.\n\nHead baseball coaches from area high schools were invited with Sullivan East's Mike Breuninger, John Battle's Jimmy Gobble, Virginia High's Adam Moore and Providence Academy's Jeff Reed among those spotted in the large crowd. Gobble and Reed both played in the majors with Reed winning a World Series ring as a catcher with the Reds in 1990.\n\nMeanwhile, Chipper Jones was visiting Bristol Motor Speedway for the first time.\n\n\"Very exciting,\" Jones said. \"I know everybody in the Braves organization is crazy jacked to get here. On a personal note, this is a place I've held high on my bucket list for a very long time.\"\n\nThe game is being held in what players call the \"dog days\" of the season, but an event that will have all the feel of a postseason game could provide a major pick-me-up.\n\n\"The routine for a major league baseball player gets kind of monotonous,\" Jones said. \"You do it all day, every day. Very seldom do you have a day off. It's good to have something to kind of break the monotony and this is the perfect instance for that. ... Right around the end of July, start of August most guys will tell you they hit a wall for about a week or 10 days where they aren't quite themselves. I feel like a break from the everyday monotony to come up here and be a part of something as special as this - every guy on that roster is going to sign up for it I promise you.\"\n\nMLB, NFL and NBA exhibition games have been held in Bristol before.\n\nThere were those aforementioned 1922 MLB exhibitions at Tenneva Field, located on what is now Commonwealth Avenue where Strongwell Corporation sits.\n\nBristol's racetrack was the home of a 1961 NFL preseason game between the Washington Redskins and Philadelphia Eagles.\n\nA 1983 NBA preseason game between the Atlanta Hawks and Cleveland Cavaliers was contested at Viking Hall.\n\nThis will be a regular season game at Bristol Motor Speedway and could provide the venue a single-game attendance record in yet another sport.\n\nTennessee's 45-24 victory over Virginia Tech on Sept. 10, 2016, in the \"Battle at Bristol\" established a college football crowd record that still stands.\n\nThe MLB mark for single-game attendance is the 115,300 who showed up at the Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum for an exhibition game between the Boston Red Sox and Los Angeles Dodgers on March 29, 2008.\n\nA regular-season doubleheader between the Cleveland Indians and New York Yankees at Municipal Stadium in Ohio apparently brought in 86,563 fans on Sept. 12, 1954. Game 5 of the 1959 World Series in Los Angeles had 92,706 people come through the turnstiles.\n\nTennessee Governor Bill Lee said there was a \"probability\" and \"likelihood\" that Bristol would own the MLB mark by this time next year.\n\nIt also could provide more momentum for the growing cause to put an MLB expansion team in Nashville.\n\nHaving the area's two most popular teams and two closest big-league teams - Atlanta and Cincinnati -playing each other will certainly put butts in the seats.\n\nHere's one connection between the two franchises that showcase the area's rich baseball heritage.\n\nClyde \"Hardrock\" Shoun of Mountain City, Tennessee, pitched for five seasons for Cincinnati and three seasons with the Boston Braves in the 1940s.\n\nHe pitched a no-hitter for the Reds on May 15, 1944, against the Braves.\n\nThe Speedway Classic could also occur a week after another major baseball milestone for the area.\n\nFormer Tazewell High School star Billy Wagner is expected to be elected to the National Baseball Hall of Fame in 2025 - the fireballing relief pitcher missed enshrinement by five votes when the most recent ballots were unveiled in January - and induction day is set for July 27, 2025, in Cooperstown, New York.\n\nPerhaps the Southwest Virginia native could throw out the first pitch at BMS as he closed out his stellar 16-year big-league career with the Braves in 2010.\n\n\"I think it would be awesome to throw out the first pitch but I'm sure there are much better options,\" Wagner said on Thursday in a telephone interview.\n\nWagner had been to BMS before.\n\n\"Of course,\" Wagner said. \"Was a big fan of [NASCAR driver] Morgan Shepherd.\"\n\nCount him among those all in when it comes to baseball at BMS.\n\n\"Playing in front of that type of crowd will be electric,\" Wagner said.\n\nSouthwest Virginia native and ex-East Tennessee State University slugger Ed Goodson played 47 games for the Atlanta Braves in 1975 - sandwiched between stints with the San Francisco Giants and Los Angeles Dodgers during an eight-season career - and could make the trip from his home in Grayson County, Virginia.\n\n\"I have never been to any events there,\" Goodson said. \"I got to see it quite a few times on my trips to and from Ivanhoe [Virginia] to ETSU when I was in college. ... I would be interested in attending the game if I can get [son] Kirk [Goodson], my son-in-law, and my three grandsons to go.\"\n\nVirginia High graduate Justin Grimm won a World Series in 2010 while pitching for the Chicago Cubs and now lives in Nashville. He's saved the date.\n\n\"I love that MLB is bringing the game to the East Tennessee area,\" Grimm said. \"When I read about it, I had to do a double take and immediately text my brother [Matt] and told him to put it on the calendar. What a great way for our area to go watch a big-league ballgame.\"\n\nThe dimensions presented of the playing field on Friday included 330 feet down the lines as the diamond would be situated in one corner of the racing infield. Plenty of work is still yet to be done.\n\n\"It's going to be really fun to watch the transformation take place,\" Jones said.\n\nMLB has held regular season games at historic Rickwood Field in Birmingham, Alabama, the Field of Dreams in Dyersville, Iowa, and foreign countries in recent years.\n\nBristol Motor Speedway and Major League Baseball are attempting to turn quite a double play.\n\n\"You walk into the venue and right away you know you're in a different kind of place, something incredibly special,\" Yolkut said. \"Not only is it big on the outside, but the energy on the inside, even when it is empty, is different than any of the other places we've recently been.\"\n\nBe the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your inbox!\n\nSign up! * I understand and agree
