{"uri": "8267580983", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-09", "time": "20:28:48", "dateTime": "2024-08-09T20:28:48Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-09T20:28:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5686274766921997, "url": "https://heraldcourier.com/double-play/article_56c69b36-5688-11ef-a0ab-c7883a028742.html", "title": "Double play", "body": "ALLEN GREGORY | BRISTOL HERALD COURIER\n\nBRISTOL, Tenn. - It's baseball time in Tennessee.\n\nFollowing years of planning and months of rumors, official confirmation of a Major League Baseball game at Bristol Motor Speedway came Friday morning during an elaborate press conference inside the 147,000-seat stadium.\n\nThe MLB Speedway Classic pitting the Cincinnati Reds and the Atlanta Braves will be held next year on Saturday, Aug. 2. FOX will provide national television coverage of the 7 p.m. contest.\n\n\"We are just thrilled to be here,\" BMS president and general manager Jerry Caldwell said. \"This has been a wonderful collaboration with our friends at Major League Baseball to get to this undertaking.\"\n\nThe press conference, televised live on the Major League Baseball Network, featured dignitaries from the worlds of baseball, NASCAR and politics.\n\nPeople are also reading... Memories lead many to Lebanon's Bonanza Steakhouse HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: Not yet 30, Norris achieves goal as Lebanon head coach PREP VOLLEYBALL: Four-time defending region champ Gate City will have new coach this season as Reed steps down Platter & Pour working to open State Street location HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL | Trust and obey: Former Sullivan East star Laisure now playing for Science Hill Hilltoppers PREP BASKETBALL: Field released for The Classic at Tennessee High PREP FOOTBALL: J.I. Burton looking for Raider revival after struggles of 2023 Antiques showcased at Virginia Highlands Festival HIGH SCHOOL NOTEBOOK: Wise Central's Emmah McAmis on Under Armour national title team; Some transfers and new coaching hires as well HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: Smith aims high for Ridgeview LOCAL MOTORSPORTS: Chilhowie racer knows the Bristol Motor Speedway experience VHSL PRESEASON FOOTBALL PRIMER: Plenty of storylines as prep football begins in Virginia PREP FOOTBALL: Wise County Central's Owen Amos returns from injury BRIEFS: Tommy Buzzo steps down as E&H's defensive coordinator Trail town now boasts pathway lined with artwork\n\nFrom college football and major concerts to dirt racing, BMS has hosted a number of unique attractions. Organizers are hoping that Speedway Classic will set an all-time attendance record for Major League Baseball.\n\nThe current MLB attendance record of 115,300 was set in 2008 at the Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum for an exhibition contest between the Boston Red Sox and Los Angeles Dodgers.\n\nMarcus Smith is the President and CEO of Speedway Motorsports, which owns BMS and other NASCAR tracks.\n\n\"We love these special events, and I think this event is going to be a lot of fun for both NASCAR fans and Major League Baseball fans,\" Smith said.\n\nSince the ambitious concept was first proposed, followers of both sports have debated just how a temporary baseball diamond can be constructed around a 0.533-concrete oval track.\n\nSteve Swift is the senior vice-president of operations and development for Speedway Motorsports. He's been the mastermind for many bold projects at BMS and other Speedway Motorsports tracks, including the revival of once-dormant North Wilkesboro Speedway.\n\n\"This is amazing,\" Swift said. \"We've been blessed to work with Marcus, and his father Bruton always had big dreams. We've been known for firsts and baseball is another first.\"\n\nThe 2016 Battle at Bristol football game between the University of Tennessee and Virginia Tech attracted an NCAA record crowd of 156,990.\n\n\"The football game was a huge undertaking and the baseball game just adds to that legacy,\" Swift said. \"Having challenges like this is what keeps us going. Working to make events happen is special to me.\"\n\nSeveral alterations will be made to the BMS infield, but Swift said the screen for the massive Colossus TV will stay in place.\n\n\"We've talked to the engineers and some of the cables for the screen are just safety precautions, so we could take those down,\" Swift said.\n\nSwift said home plate will be located at the current start-finish line for NASCAR races on the pit side. A fan zone area will be designated at one end of the infield.\n\nA portion of the road wall will be removed along with the Goodyear tire building.\n\nAccording to Swift, the baseball makeover will begin after the 2025 Spring race. The 2025 NASCAR schedule has not been released, but no changes are expected in the BMS race dates.\n\n\"The great part is that we will have plenty of time on the front end of the work,\" Swift said. \"The crunch time to turn the track around will be heading into our September race.\"\n\nSeveral renderings of the makeshift field were on display Friday along with an outline of the proposed field.\n\nThe dimensions will be 400 feet to center, 375 to right field and 384 to left.\n\nSwift said talks for the MLB-NASCAR marriage have been underway for 3-4 years.\n\n\"There has been a lot of conversation around this, and now things can finally start happening,\" Swift said.\n\nNASCAR Cup Series regulars Chase Elliott and Ross Chastain and former Cup regular Kevin Harvick took part in a ceremonial first-pitch along with former MLB greats Eric Davis of the Reds and Hall of Famer Chipper Jones of the Braves.\n\n\"It was really cool to take Chipper around the track for a couple of laps,\" Elliott said. \"I'm a Braves fan and I grew up watching the team. It's an honor for me to help promote this event.\"\n\nElliott said he hopes to attend the game.\n\n\"I'm not sure what my schedule looks like next year but I guarantee that whoever attends will have a really great experience,\" Elliott said. \"Bristol is one of the best facilities we come to each year, and everybody in this industry will tell you the same thing.\"\n\nTennessee Gov. Bill Lee said the first MLB contest in Tennessee history will have a major economic impact across the region and state.\n\n\"History will be made here,\" Lee said.\n\nTicket sales for the general public begin in December, but season-ticket holders from both teams and BMS will have first access in September. No ticket price was announced.\n\nA date of Aug. 3 has been set aside for a rain makeup.\n\nagregory@bristolnews.com | Twitter: @Greg_BHCSports | (276) 645-2544\n\nBe the first to know\n\nGet local {"uri": "8267561217", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-09", "time": "20:08:24", "dateTime": "2024-08-09T20:08:24Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-09T20:07:52Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5372549295425415, "url": "https://sports.yahoo.com/major-league-baseball-host-braves-110834561.html", "title": "Major League Baseball to host Braves, Reds at Bristol in 2025", "body": "BRISTOL, Tenn. -- Major League Baseball is heading to Thunder Valley.\n\nBristol Motor Speedway will host the \"MLB Speedway Classic\" on Aug. 2, 2025, a regular-season baseball game between the Atlanta Braves and Cincinnati Reds, MLB Vice President of Global Events Jeremiah Yolkut announced at the track Friday.\n\nThe milestone announcement marks a meshing of the baseball and racing worlds in its most unique fashion yet.\n\n\"I think it's an amazing opportunity -- and it's already begun -- to see NASCAR and MLB pull together,\" Jerry Caldwell, president and general manager of Bristol Motor Speedway, said Friday. \"I think this is a great platform for that. I think our fan bases fit naturally together, but I think we can do a lot of fun things to expose folks to both sides of that.\"\n\nRELATED: Start your engines and buy tickets here!\n\nRepresenting the NASCAR contingent at the 0.533-mile bullring race track were drivers Chase Elliott, Ross Chastain and analyst Kevin Harvick along with Speedway Motorsports president and CEO Marcus Smith, while Atlanta Braves legend Chipper Jones and Reds legend Eric Davis joined to represent their respective former teams. Elliott, the 2020 NASCAR Cup Series champion, is a longtime Braves fan hailing from Dawsonville, Georgia, with Jones a NASCAR fan dating back decades.\n\nFriday, though, marked Jones' first time inside the \"Last Great Colosseum\" before taking hot laps as a passenger in a stock car with Elliott. The mammoth stadium -- albeit a short track by NASCAR's standards -- took Jones aback despite having attended multiple Daytona 500s as a Florida native just 20 miles inland from the \"World Center of Racing.\"\n\n\"I think if you had a camera on me, my mouth would have been wide open,\" Jones said of his initial reaction to Bristol, imagining the tens of racing haulers packed into the center of the track. \"I think seeing these stands full -- being from the South and knowing what NASCAR means to everybody in the South, seeing all these butts in the seats and how loud it gets and just the bumping for four hours.\n\n\"Like I said, my pucker factor was a 9.5, and it was just me and him (Elliott) out there, you know? I mean, can you imagine 38, 39 other cars in such close proximity? All professional athletes stand in awe of professional athletes in other sports, and like no other, I stand in amazement at what these guys do.\"\n\nYolkut has led numerous global projects in his time with the MLB, including events at the historic Rickwood Field in Alabama and the MLB London Series at London Stadium in England. With a keen eye for big events, Yolkut sought a big venue that brought its own history. Enter Bristol.\n\n\"It all starts with an idea,\" Yolkut said. \"And for many years, a lot of folks within our organization and some of our partner organizations brought up the concept of playing at a large-scale sporting venue. And there's not a lot of places that can host Major League Baseball. Our diamond obviously is unique -- much different than some of the other sports. And so you really have to be strategic about what places you look at.\n\n\"But Bristol kept coming up as a possibility. And a few years ago, we came down here to take a look at it. And as Jerry mentioned in his commentary, you walk into the venue and right away, you know you're in a different kind of place, something incredibly special. Not only is it big on the outside, but the energy that's on the inside, even when it's empty, is different than any of the places that we've recently been, and that's something you're looking to make true.\"\n\nYolkut said MLB will work with BaAM Productions, BrightView and Populous as it has in past builds to create the layout of the playing field and \"allow us to bring these sites to life and figure out ways in which you can put a baseball diamond on an infield track with a giant scoreboard in the middle, and then bring in tens of thousands of fans to watch that and create that environment.\"\n\n\"So, with those folks, as well as the folks here at Bristol, we have no doubt that we will be able to work through all the various things that will come up over the next year,\" Yolkut said. \"But for the most part, a good amount of the planning is done, and now it's a matter of executing on that plan and building a diamond here in August of 2025.\"\n\nMurray Cook, leading BrightView's field design and construction, acknowledged the challenges of fitting an MLB diamond with the confines of the Bristol footprint, noting a portion of the Goodyear building inside Turns 1 and 2 will need to be removed in addition to several pit walls. He added the build is expected to take 30 days with an anticipated start on July 1, 2025.\n\n\"We've got a good design laid out as far as the actual dimensions of the park,\" Cook said. \"Got 330 (feet) down the lines and 400 to center. We got 375 to the right field alley, which is going to require part of the building out there to be removed, and we're 384 (feet) to the left field alley. So we've got good dimensions all the way around, very respectable to any major-league park in the US.\n\n\"I think that, from a construction standpoint and planning, you know, again, there's a lot of leveling needs to be done as you mentioned, and our goal there is to level that up with gravel like they typically would under the baseball fields and soccer fields that they use synthetic turf on. And obviously that's also creating a large drainage issue with the actual infield pit area, so we're putting a lot of drainage. So we're in the engineering process to get that buttoned up. But again, we're on a good path and got some good local partners here to work with.\"\n\nElliott, NASCAR's six-time defending Most Popular Driver, has long rooted for the Braves and was rewarded for it as a fan in 2021 as the Braves stormed to its first World Series title since 1995. In fact, Elliott even pulled his own version of double-duty as a driver-fan on Halloween that year, leading 289 laps at Martinsville Speedway, qualifying for the Championship 4 and then flying home to Dawsonville while the Braves played the Houston Astros in Game 5 with a 3-1 series advantage.\n\n\"I had some tickets, and I wasn't sure whether or not I was gonna go,\" Elliott recalled, \"and I had decided coming home I was pretty tired and I wasn't gonna go. And I was driving to my house, and I was listening on radio, and (Adam Duvall) hit a four-run home run there early in the game. ... And they would have won the series that night if they had won. And I was like, oh my gosh, they just hit this home run. I'm gonna have to go. So I took a right, went south, and I showed up down there, and they ended up blowing the game. But they got it back a couple nights later. It was pretty fun, though.\"\n\nThe ties between baseball and racing run deep, and that has perhaps never been more true than Friday's announcement. And while it's a baseball game on deck at Bristol, Chastain sees beauty on both sides of the proverbial coin.\n\nMORE: How to get notified for 2025 schedule release\n\n\"I think it's unmeasurable what it could do for both sports,\" Chastain said. \"People coming here may have never even heard of Bristol, but they're coming for the baseball game. And Bristol season-ticket holders might think, 'You know what? I went to the football game. I went to the dirt sprint car races and the dirt races here and a bunch of NASCAR races. I want to go see a baseball game here.' I think you're gonna have quite a bit of cross-pollination with that.\"\n\nIndeed, the \"World's Fastest Half-Mile\" housed the 2016 \"Battle at Bristol,\" a regular-season college football contest between the University of Tennessee and Virginia Tech, a game that drew an NCAA football record crowd of 156,990 people to the \"Last Great Colosseum.\"\n\nThe track additionally hosted an NCAA FCS football game between East Tennessee State and Western Carolina one week after the \"Battle of Bristol,\" while the National Football League played an exhibition football game at Bristol between Philadelphia and Washington in 1961.\n\nWhat's set to come in 2025, however, is something entirely new. The facility has never played host to professional baseball, and the state of Tennessee has never hosted an MLB game. Now, two franchises steeped in history are set to write a new chapter within the concrete oval next year.", "source": {"uri": "sports.yahoo.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Yahoo Sports"}, The game will be between the Atlanta Braves and Cincinnati Reds; both cities a just shy of a 5-hour drive from the speedway.\n\nBristol sits on the Tennessee-Virginia border, about 115 miles north of Gatlinburg. The official announcement of the matchup from MLB is reportedly expected to come Friday.\n\nWith this game, a new baseball attendance record could be set.\n\nBristol Motor Speedway has a capacity of 153,000 for car racing, and depending on how the field is built and the seating is situated, it could be the place where the largest crowd to watch an MLB game has ever gathered.\n\nCurrently, depending on how you want to look at it, there are actually two records. And no, this doesn't involve an asterisk like Roger Maris' home run record.\n\nThe most recent record was set at the Los Angeles Coliseum in 2008 when the Los Angeles Dodgers and Boston Red Sox drew 115,300 spectators for a pre-season exhibition game.\n\nThe season marked 50 years since the Dodgers moved to LA from Brooklyn in 1958, and since the team was housed in the LA Coliseum until Dodger Stadium opened in 1962, the Dodgers made a nostalgic return to the facility.\n\nBut some may say that's not the official record. After all, the game was an exhibition - not exactly what some would call an \"official\" game since it didn't take place during the regular season.\n\nThat particular record belongs to the Colorado Rockies.\n\nWhen baseball expanded by two teams in 1993 (the Florida Marlins were the other franchise), the Rockies stadium, Coors Field, wasn't complete and wouldn't be for the next two years. Thus, the team shared old Mile High Stadium, which was multipurpose and housed previous minor league baseball teams, but it is forever known as the home of the NFL's Denver Broncos.\n\nThe Rockies played the Montreal Expos (now the Washington Nationals) on April 9, 1993 to a crowd of 84,087.\n\nAnd this isn't the first time Major League Baseball has ventured out of the cities of its 30 teams to play games.\n\nMLB has hosted games in London, Japan, Australia and Mexico. The league has also hosted games at the legendary Rickwood Field in Birmingham, Alabama; at the site of the \"Field of Dreams\" filming location in Iowa and Fort Bragg in North Carolina - the first time an MLB game took place on an active military base.\n\nThere was even a game played in Hawaii in 1997 at Aloha Stadium.\n\nThe San Diego Padres ballpark at the time, Qualcomm Stadium (Jack Murphy Stadium to purists) was undergoing renovations and was not ready for the start of the baseball season. So the Padres' series against the St. Louis Cardinals was moved to Aloha Stadium - better known as the longtime home of the NFL Pro Bowl - but like so may others was a multipurpose facility for both sports.\n\nOther sports have had their moments in different places too.\n\nNCAA basketball was played on the deck of the USS Carl Vinson aircraft carrier and the NH hosts the Stadium Series and Winter However, every once in a while, a unique opportunity presents itself to the venue, and the stadium trades out its race cars for another sporting event.\n\nThis time around, the Bristol, Tennessee racetrack will transform into a baseball diamond. The Athletic first reported that the 150,000 seat stadium will be the host of a neutral site game between the Cincinnati Reds and the Atlanta Braves in 2025.\n\nThe two national league teams will have similar travel times to the racetrack that's almost smack dab in the middle of their homes. For Atlanta, they'll have to travel around four hours from their usual place of play, and for Cincinnati, they'll face a five hour drive to get to Bristol.\n\nWith the two teams matching up at a neutral site, it should give fans a chance to \"meet in the middle\" and go see their favorite team there instead of driving all the way to one place or the other. At the very least, baseball fans will be treated to a classic game of baseball in a stadium that's much different than what a regular ball park looks like.\n\nAnd it's not the first time that the speedway was converted to fulfill another purpose. Back in 2016, Virginia Tech and Tennessee played a game there, and set the record for highest attended NCAA football game with 156,990 fans in attendance.\n\nThe regular season game is set to be played at Bristol Motor Speedway on August 2nd of 2025. An official announcement is expected to be released this Friday at a planned news conference at the racetrack.\n\nIf all goes according to plan, it will be the first ever in-season Major League The New York Giants' old ballpark in Harlem was shaped like an oval, with foul lines that were 277 feet down left field and 258 down right.\n\n\"And center was, like, 500, right?\" Moll said.\n\nThe Athletic was first Tuesday with the report of the latest in a series MLB games staged at unique venues, including the 2022 Field of Dreams game in Dyersville, Iowa, featuring the Reds and Chicago Cubs. A formal announcement is expected Friday.\n\nThis first-of-its kind baseball stage presents the opportunity for the Reds and Braves to set a record for single-game baseball attendance, given the potential for seating capacity of more than 150,000.\n\nMLB's all-time attendance mark is 115,300 for a 2008 game at the Los Angeles Coliseum between the Dodgers and Boston Red Sox, according to the Athletic report. Bristol hosted a college football game between nearby University of Tennessee and Virginia Tech that drew an American football record 156,990.\n\n\"I've never bene to Bristol. But I've been to Daytona,\" said Reds pitcher Carson Spiers, a South Carolina native, who has become a NASCAR fan just this year, thanks to a sort of fantasy league he and some former Louisville teammates put together.\n\n\"That's sweet,\" he said. \"It'll be fun.\"\n\nSpiers has one request: that favorite driver Ty Gibbs show up. \"Tell him to come,\" Spiers said.\n\nIf Gibbs does, maybe he can help settle what's sure to be a burning question.
